  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_550f9df0-c7c0-4698-b6cd-c0a9bd55c0b1'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12509448960280161982"><em>Under Wildwood </em>is the second book in the <em>New York Times</em> bestselling adventure series the Wildwood Chronicles from Colin Meloy, lead singer of the Decemberists, and Carson Ellis, the acclaimed illustrator of <em>The Mysterious Benedict Society</em>.<br/><br/>Ever since Prue McKeel returned home from the Impassable Wilderness after rescuing her brother from the malevolent Dowager Governess, li</span>
  <span id="freeText12509448960280161982" style="display:none"><em>Under Wildwood </em>is the second book in the <em>New York Times</em> bestselling adventure series the Wildwood Chronicles from Colin Meloy, lead singer of the Decemberists, and Carson Ellis, the acclaimed illustrator of <em>The Mysterious Benedict Society</em>.<br /><br />Ever since Prue McKeel returned home from the Impassable Wilderness after rescuing her brother from the malevolent Dowager Governess, life has been pretty dull. School holds no interest for her, and her new science teacher keeps getting on her case about her dismal test scores and daydreaming in class. Her mind is constantly returning to the verdant groves and sky-tall trees of Wildwood, where her friend Curtis still remains as a bandit-in-training.<br /><br />But all is not well in that world. Dark assassins with mysterious motives conspire to settle the scores of an unknown client. A titan of industry employs inmates from his orphanage to work his machine shop, all the while obsessing over the exploitation of the Impassable Wilderness. And, in what will be their greatest challenge yet, Prue and Curtis are thrown together again to save themselves and the lives of their friends, and to bring unity to a divided country. But in order to do that, they must go under Wildwood.<br /><br />In <em>Under Wildwood</em>, Colin Meloy and Carson Ellis reveal new dimensions of the epic fantasy-adventure series begun with the critically acclaimed, bestselling <em>Wildwood</em>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12509448960280161982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2902743229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3063012553223669883"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567377524i/28085735._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><i>Sometimes, when the world is falling apart around you, all that's left to do is dance, right?</i>
</blockquote>Prue McKeel saved her brother, <b>led Wildwood to freedom</b> and fought her way back to the normal world. <br/><br/>But somehow, even though all she wanted to do was return to her parents...things just don't feel the same.<blockquote>
  <i>School holds no interest for her...her mind is constantly returning to the verdant groves and sky-tall trees of Wildwood...</i>
</blockquote>Curtis, Prue's best friend, spends his time in bandit training in the I</span>
  <span id="freeText3063012553223669883" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567377524i/28085735._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>Sometimes, when the world is falling apart around you, all that's left to do is dance, right?</i>
</blockquote>Prue McKeel saved her brother, <b>led Wildwood to freedom</b> and fought her way back to the normal world. <br><br>But somehow, even though all she wanted to do was return to her parents...things just don't feel the same.<blockquote>
  <i>School holds no interest for her...her mind is constantly returning to the verdant groves and sky-tall trees of Wildwood...</i>
</blockquote>Curtis, Prue's best friend, spends his time in bandit training in the Impassable Wilderness - and all Prue can think about is how much she wishes to be there too.<br><br>And then the assassin shows up, and she really has <b>no choice but to return.</b><br><br>Meanwhile Curtis's parents are beside themselves and when rumors reach them that Curtis is in Turkey, they drop off his two younger sisters at the local orphanage in order to travel there.<br><br>But the<b> orphanage is not what it seems. </b>There's a sinister scientist determined to break through the Impassable Wilderness and into Wildwood - and the girls are trapped right in the middle of itall. <blockquote>
  <i>I just saw her. She was so … alive.</i>
</blockquote>Throughout all of this, there is something <b>menacing brewing in the heart of the Impassible Wilderness </b>- and the children will have no choice but to confront it themselves.<br><br>All in all - this was <b>a rather good sequel. </b><br><br>I liked the continuation of the series and the direction it took.<br><br>The<b> addition of Curtis's sisters </b>(and their misadventures) was a good touch. It is often so hard to introduce new main characters but Meloy did it smoothly and effortlessly.<br><br>I do feel that some of the characterizations (in particular, when Prue and Curtis disagreed) <b>seemed inconsistent</b> with the first book. <br><br>Well, maybe not inconsistent, but more like exaggerated? Things that would have not bothered them before seem to be <b>VERY BIG DEALS</b> this round, which seemed a smidge out of a character.<br><br>However, the adventure was really well written.<br><br>I loved exploring the various <b>ins and outs of Wildwood</b> and the Imapssable Wilderness with thee whole gang - that was so much fun (and absolutely fascinating!).<br><br>The one thing that was a bit of a hangup for me was that <b>this book was over 550 pages </b>(which to me on audiobook) wasn't too terrible, but it does seem rather long for a middle grade book. <br><br>As a big book lover, I didn't have much of an issue, but it can be a bit of a barrier for some kids. <br><br>All in all - this sequel delivered and I cannot wait to get my hands on the third!!<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Narrated by the author - very impressive! I always love when the author reads their own book.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3063012553223669883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8035193-sarah?shelf=youngfolk">youngfolk</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer503689095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8665063303503325066">THANK GOODNESS IT'S OVER!!!!!!!!!!!<br/><br/>I don't know why I kept reading. I normally take pride in giving up on a book I'm not enjoying. I am in charge of my reading life! I don't let guilt propel me! There are too many great books I'll never read to waste time on those I don't like. <br/><br/>Why did I keep on reading this one even though I was not enjoying it?<br/>1. I enjoyed the first one. I assume it's going to be a trilogy and I like reading trilogies. 3 is the magic number!<br/>2. I like the look and feel of the b</span>
  <span id="freeText8665063303503325066" style="display:none">THANK GOODNESS IT'S OVER!!!!!!!!!!!<br /><br />I don't know why I kept reading. I normally take pride in giving up on a book I'm not enjoying. I am in charge of my reading life! I don't let guilt propel me! There are too many great books I'll never read to waste time on those I don't like. <br /><br />Why did I keep on reading this one even though I was not enjoying it?<br />1. I enjoyed the first one. I assume it's going to be a trilogy and I like reading trilogies. 3 is the magic number!<br />2. I like the look and feel of the books. The illustrations are lovely.<br />3. It's a mythologized version of my own city, nearby neighborhoods and the Forrest Park wooded area that crowns Portland.<br />4. My husband bought it for me for Christmas. I like getting books for Christmas.<br />5. It seemed like I would enjoy it if I would just straighten up my attitude.<br /><br />I was bored. It was tedious. There was no heart. I thought the underworld would be more like an underworld (more banished souls and/or a devil character and less moles.) The Portland references (including the Shanghai Tunnels) and a nod to our Pabst Blue Ribbon hipster culture only made me roll my eyes. And now it's over and it was such an unsatisfying non-conclusion, which means that there will be no closure unless I read the 3rd and final installment. I don't wanna. I'll read the Cliff's Notes but that's it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8665063303503325066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2268724741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2268724741" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475352701p2/45261627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2268724741?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=as-it-began">as-it-began</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=all-ages-admitted">all-ages-admitted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=because-robots">because-robots</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=the-deep-places-of-the-world">the-deep-places-of-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=the-woods">the-woods</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=super-sisters">super-sisters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=pretty-black-cover">pretty-black-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=almost-gothic-in-a-natural-way">almost-gothic-in-a-natural-way</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2268724741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13393224859768454252">Congratulations, Colin Meloy, for producing a second installment that was noticeably better than the first!<br/><br/>A few months after Prue McKeel and Curtis Mehlberg entered the Impassible Wilderness to rescue Prue’s baby brother from an evil sorceress, life has returned to mostly normal for the McKeel family, although Prue is struggling in school and her parents don’t know why. The Mehlbergs have had no such luck. Curtis is still missing, and the parents are so desperate to find him that they flew to T</span>
  <span id="freeText13393224859768454252" style="display:none">Congratulations, Colin Meloy, for producing a second installment that was noticeably better than the first!<br><br>A few months after Prue McKeel and Curtis Mehlberg entered the Impassible Wilderness to rescue Prue’s baby brother from an evil sorceress, life has returned to mostly normal for the McKeel family, although Prue is struggling in school and her parents don’t know why. The Mehlbergs have had no such luck. Curtis is still missing, and the parents are so desperate to find him that they flew to Turkey, leaving their two daughters, Rachel and Elsie, at the decidedly creepy Unthank Home for Wayward Youth.<br><br>Meanwhile Curtis has been happily training as a bandit in the Wildwood, almost never remembering his parents and sisters. The mad Dowager Governess was defeated (although we all know the drill with fantasy “deaths” without a body to show for it) leaving chaos in the wood. Warring factions have sprung up and no one seems to know who the leader should be. Iphigenia, Chief Mystic and priestess of the Great Tree, insists that Prue needs to come back if the Wood should be saved. The girl’s destiny has not yet run its course.<br><br>Back in Portland, Prue confides in a concerned new teacher, Ms. Thennis. Prue suspects the Wood is calling her back, but what’s wrong now?<br><br><b>Content Advisory</b><br><i>Violence</i>: Like the first book—not much, but what’s there is startlingly bloody for a middle-grade book. We see a shape-shifter get stabbed, and her shape changes from her human to animal form as it dies. Assassins are sent after children, and while they are unsuccessful, that’s not for lack of effort or menace on their part. Joffrey Unthank forces children to labor in his factory, and some have been maimed or terribly injured in said factory. Some rebellious kids burn down a building.<br><br><i>Sex</i>: Prue notices that Curtis’ shoulders are starting to broaden. That’s it.<br><br><i>Language</i>: None.<br><br><i>Substance Abuse</i>: None.<br><br><i>Nightmare Fuel</i>: The aforementioned shape-shifter is described in a frightening way, and one of the illustrations portraying her in mid-morph gave me the willies. That said, it’s a lot less scary than the first book. Know your kids. Kids, know yourselves.<br><br><i>Miscellaneous</i>: There’s a villainous Ukrainian character who speaks in a stereotypical accent and generally acts like an evil agent from the <i>Rocky &amp; Bullwinkle</i> cartoon. She’s not super offensive, but she still comes off as a product of accidental xenophobia.<br><br><b>Conclusions</b><br>The first volume in the Wildwood series, simply entitled <i>Wildwood</i>, really rubbed me the wrong way for a variety of reasons. The characters were hard to empathize with, the story took too long to get where it was going, and the whole thing was so hipster it had never heard of itself. Not to mention that the narrator’s fondness for obscure vocabulary words made it hard to picture what was happening at some points. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525796511ra/25505217.gif" width="500" height="271" alt="Paul and George HDN" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However, the book had a lot of potential. It stole from the best—<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1069006.C_S__Lewis" title="C.S. Lewis" rel="nofollow noopener">C.S. Lewis</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4427.Jim_Henson" title="Jim Henson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jim Henson</a>, and a wee dash of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/656983.J_R_R__Tolkien" title="J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">J.R.R. Tolkien</a> at the end—while bringing its own Old Americana aesthetic and an agreeably spooky mood. The illustrations by Carson Ellis (who happens to be Meloy’s wife and album-cover artist) were charming pieces of folk art. The first book dashed my hopes, but for some reason the second one called to me. And while not the greatest general-audience fantasy novel ever written, it’s actually quite agreeable. <br><br>The addition of Joffrey Unthank and his orphanage/factory is straight outta <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/36746.Lemony_Snicket" title="Lemony Snicket" rel="nofollow noopener">Lemony Snicket</a>, which both is and isn’t an improvement on the first book. It’s an improvement because a lot of the weirder “real world” parts make sense if the “real world” in this universe is a Snicketesque realm of absurdism. Yet it’s also a step back because there was no indication in book one that this world was like that. It’s a good ret-con, but still a ret-con. And even in such a surreal place, Mom and Dad Mehlberg leaving their two remaining children in such a place while they go to search for their son doesn’t jive with what little we know about them. Violet, Klaus and Sunny Baudelaire wound up in situations this bad and worse, but their parents were <i>dead</i>. Big difference.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525797021ra/25505257.gif" width="500" height="270" alt="Violet, Klaus and Sunny" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>On a related note, the almost bloodless battle between the kids and the Industrial Titans’ goons was underwhelming after the spectacle at the Plinth in the first book, wherein people actually died and there were fantastical creatures. This one felt a little too much like the end of a '90s family comedy. It just did not go with the tone of the previous book, or this one up until that point. <br><br>As for the Titans themselves, Big Business being the villain has become cliché, but it usually doesn’t share antagonist duties with faceless magical forces, so watching the heroes battle both in <i>Wildwood Imperium</i> should actually be interesting.<br><br>The hipster milieu from the first book has also been greatly toned down. It has receded to the background, where it’s just fine. Prue and Curtis no longer try to wriggle out of their destined duties, and they certainly aren’t ranting anymore about emotional support while everyone else is marching off to die. They have figured out that pacifism is a good policy in Portland, but will not save you from an evil sorceress or a shape-shifting assassin. When one lives in two different worlds, one can accommodate two different world<i>views</i>. <br><br>Also no more posturing about expensive jeans or coffee. They were actually believable twelve-year-olds this time around. And Curtis got called out for being selfish and oblivious—by Prue, by the narrator, and by his own conscience. Character development. It’s a good thing.<br><br>Rachel and Elsie, Curtis’ sisters, are not terribly unique—Rachel is a typical sulky goth teen, Elsie is a typical bright-eyed little girl who brings her doll everywhere—but they were believable and likeable enough. They reminded me of both Susan and Lucy Pevensie from Narnia, and Wirt and Greg from <i>Over the Garden Wall</i>. Both very nice sets of sibling characters to be reminded of.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525796510ra/25505213.gif" width="500" height="213" alt="Susan and Lucy" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525796510ra/25505214.gif" width="500" height="276" alt="Wirt and Greg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>The most interesting new addition to the ensemble hasn’t even shown up yet. Remember Alexei, son of Alexandra? When he died, she went mad with grief and forced two Daedalus-like geniuses to rebuild him as an automaton, only for Alexei to figure out what he really was and destroy himself. Well, Prue has been told by the Great Tree that her task is to revive Alexei somehow, that only this can save the Wood. <br><br>Some reviewers think this refers to an act of dark magic, and while it might, I can see another possibility: Prue must descend into this universe’s Land of the Dead, find Alexei, and help him “return to the Sunlit Lands” (h/t <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/65641.The_Silver_Chair__Chronicles_of_Narnia___4_" title="The Silver Chair (Chronicles of Narnia, #4) by C.S. Lewis" rel="nofollow noopener">The Silver Chair</a>
</i>). I really hope this is what Meloy means: the descent and return of figures like Persephone, Dionysus, Orpheus and Psyche are some of the most potent stories in all of mythology. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525796511i/25505215.jpg" width="366" height="504" alt="Leighton Persephone Returns" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>All told, this was a decent book, much better than I expected one in this series to be, and my curiosity is piqued for the third and final installment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13393224859768454252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3307763127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8078158654197940050"><i>“Sometimes, when the world is falling apart around you, all that's left to do is dance, right?”</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533320729ra/26072286.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>When I finished reading the first book in this series, I wasn't very involved with it, and actually found it pretty dry. However, I recognized the talent of the author and thought the second book was worth a try. I am so glad I did! This might be one of those rare cases in which book number two in a series is actually better than the first one. Even though the characters and setting are pretty much th</span>
  <span id="freeText8078158654197940050" style="display:none"><i>“Sometimes, when the world is falling apart around you, all that's left to do is dance, right?”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533320729ra/26072286.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>When I finished reading the first book in this series, I wasn't very involved with it, and actually found it pretty dry. However, I recognized the talent of the author and thought the second book was worth a try. I am so glad I did! This might be one of those rare cases in which book number two in a series is actually better than the first one. Even though the characters and setting are pretty much the same, the pacing in this one is much faster, the action is less about battles and more about adventure, and there's a whole "orphans doing cool things" trope that gave me Lemony Snicket's vibes. I guess this is a series worth finishing, after all!!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_530362884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/530362884" />
    <a title="Ingrid" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4303543-ingrid"><img alt="Ingrid" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434861230p2/4303543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/530362884?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ingrid" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ingrid" href="/user/show/4303543-ingrid">Ingrid</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer530362884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8176143216143946467">My goodness Colin Meloy turned this series around! At the end of the last one, I was pleased. It seemed like a good, happy way to wrap things up (ignoring the fact that Curtis never went home. I didn't agree with that.) However, in this second book, he takes the book to a much darker level. People die. Hands are cut off. Both of these things I tend to appreciate in books. <br/><br/>Anyway, despite (or perhaps because of) the darker feel to this book, I really enjoyed it. It was exciting, it was unique, an</span>
  <span id="freeText8176143216143946467" style="display:none">My goodness Colin Meloy turned this series around! At the end of the last one, I was pleased. It seemed like a good, happy way to wrap things up (ignoring the fact that Curtis never went home. I didn't agree with that.) However, in this second book, he takes the book to a much darker level. People die. Hands are cut off. Both of these things I tend to appreciate in books. <br /><br />Anyway, despite (or perhaps because of) the darker feel to this book, I really enjoyed it. It was exciting, it was unique, and I adore the setting. The Wildwood has such a Narnia feel to it that gives me warm fuzzies. <br /><br />The main thing that annoyed me with this book was the loong interlude in the middle.I definitely think that Meloy could have cut down some of the parts and made it a bit shorter. <br /><br />However, this was still a good book. And still a good series to read aloud to perhaps an nine or ten year old (it wasn't <i>that</i> dark, just darker than the last one.) <br /><br />I certainly look forward to the last book. (Wonder what it will be called: Over Wildwood? Through Wildwood? Wild Wildwood?)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8176143216143946467" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_423546044" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/423546044" />
    <a title="Candace Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/924490-candace-jean"><img alt="Candace Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332293814p2/924490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/423546044?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace Jean" href="/user/show/924490-candace-jean">Candace Jean</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer423546044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9250840459926402352">The overall feeling/aura/context of Under Wildwood matches it's cover: dark.<br/><br/>Dark places, dark emotion, and very dark verbiage. Meloy definitely took this story to depths not seen in the first book, and he approached bloodshed with zero fluff.<br/><br/>Somehow the entire 559 pages are spent merely aligning things for the third book, though a hearty amount of new characters are introduced and new places explored. <br/><br/>Unfortunately I was turned off almost immediately by WAY too many "hold ups" in the book.. mean</span>
  <span id="freeText9250840459926402352" style="display:none">The overall feeling/aura/context of Under Wildwood matches it's cover: dark.<br /><br />Dark places, dark emotion, and very dark verbiage. Meloy definitely took this story to depths not seen in the first book, and he approached bloodshed with zero fluff.<br /><br />Somehow the entire 559 pages are spent merely aligning things for the third book, though a hearty amount of new characters are introduced and new places explored. <br /><br />Unfortunately I was turned off almost immediately by WAY too many "hold ups" in the book.. meaning.. characters kept saying the phrase "Hold up" instead of "wait a minute", "hold on" or even "just a second", and for some reason it really irritated me. It seemed Meloy tried too hard to find a "tween" voice at parts in order to relate to pre-teen readers, but it wasn't necessary as he pulled off Wildwood (book 1) in his own words and it worked wonderfully. <br /><br />Also too many "could only be described as"es and backpedaling paragraphs to defend a thought or situation that the reader probably already remembered from previous narrative. <br /><br />In the end and all negatives aside, Meloy's written style won me over again. I prefer the first book to this one, but Under Wildwood still craftily carried me off to the magic places and characters of the series that I love reading about. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9250840459926402352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/537070060?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/1559491-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1559491-sam?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer537070060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17385950599817283443"><b>2.5</b><br/><br/>It's weird to be saying this, but I did not enjoy <i>Under Wildwood</i> as much as I did the first book. It just didn't capture me the same way, and while I didn't mind that this book was a little darker, it was lacking a spark that kept me wanting to read it every day. I did finish it, and while the prose is lovely and Prue was still a great protagonist, everything in terms of the story fell flat and didn't keep me engaged. Also, why did the moles speak in caps lock? That got really irritating afte</span>
  <span id="freeText17385950599817283443" style="display:none"><b>2.5</b><br /><br />It's weird to be saying this, but I did not enjoy <i>Under Wildwood</i> as much as I did the first book. It just didn't capture me the same way, and while I didn't mind that this book was a little darker, it was lacking a spark that kept me wanting to read it every day. I did finish it, and while the prose is lovely and Prue was still a great protagonist, everything in terms of the story fell flat and didn't keep me engaged. Also, why did the moles speak in caps lock? That got really irritating after while.<br /><br />If Meloy keeps <i>Wildwood</i> going, I know I'll still check it out. I just feel like this book may be mis-marketed in a lot of ways, as it's labelled middle grade, yet it makes references to things from the late 70s, early 80s, something I don't think this middle grader generation would pick up on or understand. I get that Meloy has some very older roots (it's very prevalent in his music, which I adore), but I feel like his style and his desire to tell a very old fashioned fairy tale with a hipster twist didn't quite pan out the way I hoped it would. <br /><br />We shall see, I love the universe Colin Meloy has created, so for all I know it could have been a "it's not you, it's me" situation. :/</span>
  <a data-text-id="17385950599817283443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_639780659" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/639780659" />
    <a title="Madeline Knight-Dixon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5518809-madeline-knight-dixon"><img alt="Madeline Knight-Dixon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308587835p2/5518809.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/639780659?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline Knight-Dixon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline Knight-Dixon" href="/user/show/5518809-madeline-knight-dixon">Madeline Knight-Dixon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer639780659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5548233259409452644">This book is just as magical and intriguing as the first one. It continues the story of the world right on the edge of our world, but this time shows the grittier side of both. Children being used for free labor, assassins of some fanatic religious group, overcoming tyrannical leaders, abandoning your family to live the life you want and the consequences that come with that. I mean I can’t think of a young adult book that does ALL this at once besides this one.<br/><br/>My favorite part is still the illus</span>
  <span id="freeText5548233259409452644" style="display:none">This book is just as magical and intriguing as the first one. It continues the story of the world right on the edge of our world, but this time shows the grittier side of both. Children being used for free labor, assassins of some fanatic religious group, overcoming tyrannical leaders, abandoning your family to live the life you want and the consequences that come with that. I mean I can’t think of a young adult book that does ALL this at once besides this one.<br /><br />My favorite part is still the illustrations though. They’re so charming, and they help bring the story to life without forcing you to imagine everything a certain way. Every few pages there will be this small image to help guide you, which makes reading it so much more fun.<br /><br />Not to mention the lessons about growing up in this book are completely unreal. I felt like I grew up just reading it, and I’m 23. No matter how old you are, you’re never too old to get slapped in the face by the reality that you’ll always have to make hard decisions, even if you run away from them. That in itself makes this book worth reading, but the awesome story (and cliffhanger!) make it a must.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="5548233259409452644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer458656946144399173">There's something about this series that brings me back for each book. I love them and hate them. They fascinate me and bore me at the same time. This book is over 500 pages and it took me almost a year to finish reading it once I had started. It's very descriptive and almost slow until suddenly it isn't. I felt that way about the first book as well. I had to make myself sit down to read it only to discover by the time I was done reading that day, I'd finished a good portion of the book. <br/>This bo</span>
  <span id="freeText458656946144399173" style="display:none">There's something about this series that brings me back for each book. I love them and hate them. They fascinate me and bore me at the same time. This book is over 500 pages and it took me almost a year to finish reading it once I had started. It's very descriptive and almost slow until suddenly it isn't. I felt that way about the first book as well. I had to make myself sit down to read it only to discover by the time I was done reading that day, I'd finished a good portion of the book. <br />This book sets up for the third and I hated that realization because I wanted to be able to leave the series behind and read something faster. I might still hold off on book three. <br /><br />Overall, the world is fun. The characters are many and interesting. The language is a little mature and not too childish for adult readers. Honestly, I don't know if a child would much like the books. They are a bit complicated. <br /><br />Random review and I feel like I'm spiraling, but that's kind of how reading the book was for me as well. So, fitting? </span>

<div id="review_2640534897" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2640534897" />
    <a title="Catherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/867628-catherine"><img alt="Catherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543303139p2/867628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=cults-and-other-alternative-lifesty">cults-and-other-alternative-lifesty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=middle-grades">middle-grades</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=despicable-people">despicable-people</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2640534897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17300475650416947033"><i>Ms. Darla Thennis, olive skin, floral dashiki, stared on from behind a lectern at the front of the room. She adjusted her wire-rim glasses and smoothed her crow-black hair. She then silenced the class with a wave of her hand. "Your project, Prue?"...<br/>"My dad," began Prue. "My dad threw it away."...<br/>Ms. Thennis peered at Prue from above her glass. "Uncool, Prue," she said. "Deeply uncool."<br/>"I'll let him know that," replied Prue. ...<br/>Darla Thennis was from Eugene and clearly prided herself on being co</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17300475650416947033" style="display:none"><i>Ms. Darla Thennis, olive skin, floral dashiki, stared on from behind a lectern at the front of the room. She adjusted her wire-rim glasses and smoothed her crow-black hair. She then silenced the class with a wave of her hand. "Your project, Prue?"...<br />"My dad," began Prue. "My dad threw it away."...<br />Ms. Thennis peered at Prue from above her glass. "Uncool, Prue," she said. "Deeply uncool."<br />"I'll let him know that," replied Prue. ...<br />Darla Thennis was from Eugene and clearly prided herself on being cool, being at the kids' level. She never failed to mention to the students that she loved pop music. She made strange growling sounds every time the principal, Mr. Bream, left the room, and walked the halls engulfed in a dense cloud of patchouli.</i><br /><br />Thanks to the character of Ms. Thennis and her omnipresent dashiki, <i>Under Wildwood</i> has earned the title of "Most Uses of the Word Dashiki in a Middle Grades Novel." Also, I'm pretty sure dashiki-wearing, patchouli-smelling, Eugenite Ms. Thennis would be too cool for pop music. Seriously, Colin Meloy? Shouldn't Ms. Thennis like The Decemberists? <br /><br />After my initial read of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205221292" rel="nofollow noopener">Wildwood</a> six years ago, I didn't think I would continue the series. But after listening to the audiobook version with my family, I decided to continue as a read-aloud. It's growing on me. <br /><br />Prue has returned to her home in the St. Johns (north Portland) neighborhood, where only her toddler brother Mac has really returned to normal after his brush with death. Relations between Prue and her parents remain a bit strained, and between her adventures in the Impassible Wilderness and her newfound ability to communicate with plants, middle school feels irrelevant. <br /><br />Curtis has remained in Wildwood and is training as a bandit. He's left the Outside world behind with no regrets. But all is not well in Southwood, where the removal of the former corrupt government has left a vacuum in which many interests struggle to take control. The bandits themselves are in trouble and so is his old friend, Prue. <br /><br />And that family that Curtis so callously left behind? They've fallen apart in his absence. His parents take off to chase a lead halfway around the world, leaving his two sisters at Unthank Home for Wayward Youth, an nefarious orphanage located in the Industrial Wastes, that also takes in juvenile boarders. (Me: That's not a thing! Parents don't do that!) <br /><br />In addition to the talking animals (including my favorite -- Septimus the sarcastic rat), bandits, mystics, et al, from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10431447.Wildwood__Wildwood_Chronicles___1_" title="Wildwood (Wildwood Chronicles, #1) by Colin Meloy" rel="nofollow noopener">Wildwood</a>, book 2 has shape-shifting ninja assassins and a new cast of characters who live...under Wildwood <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ THEY'RE MOLES! ADORABLE, BLIND MOLES WHO TALK ALL IN CAPS AND HAVE BUILT A CITY OF GARBAGE!!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It's a non-stop adventure that ends with a cliff-hanger as Prue and Curtis must save everyone they care about and Wildwood itself. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17300475650416947033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13847059856396182898">This was a fun young kids story about the adventures of trying to save Wildwood. My favorite part was when Pru accidentally stepped on a mole and it yelled, “I’ve been smote!”. Of course she just moved and he was fine but that was funny.</span>

<div id="review_1219052129" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219052129" />
    <a title="Audra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2015709-audra"><img alt="Audra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1239162526p2/2015709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219052129?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Audra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Audra" href="/user/show/2015709-audra">Audra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219052129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8982713818637505543">I should have reread my review of the first one before buying the second. Geesh.<br/><br/>Once I started reading, I remembered a vague sense of not loving the series, but couldn't remember why. So, I kept reading. After about 300 pages, the "why" became clear.<br/><br/>In Middle Earth, Frodo undertakes an overwhelming odyssey, to save Middle Earth from a great evil: total domination and destruction by Sauron.<br/>In Narnia, the four children, never before trained in battle, arm and prepare to fight a great evil: the Whi</span>
  <span id="freeText8982713818637505543" style="display:none">I should have reread my review of the first one before buying the second. Geesh.<br /><br />Once I started reading, I remembered a vague sense of not loving the series, but couldn't remember why. So, I kept reading. After about 300 pages, the "why" became clear.<br /><br />In Middle Earth, Frodo undertakes an overwhelming odyssey, to save Middle Earth from a great evil: total domination and destruction by Sauron.<br />In Narnia, the four children, never before trained in battle, arm and prepare to fight a great evil: the White Witch, the curse of eternal winter, and her tyranny over all Narnians.<br />In Harry Potter, Harry is challenged again and again to over come the most evil wizard of all time, in order to save not just his friends and family, but all Muggles and Muggle-born wizards, everywhere.<br /><br />In Wildwood, Prue and Curtis (and apparently his sisters) must use their wits, wiles, and resources to fight a great evil: Industry and Capitalism. Because the Five Titans of Industry want to use the trees in the Impassable Wilderness to make money.<br /><br />I get that some people do see that as a great evil; I, too, love and support the National Parks, conservation, and wisdom with our resources. But is that a compelling basis for a 1500-page trilogy? No.<br /><br />Furthermore, and RELIGIOUS PARENTS OF CHILDREN WHO LOVE FANTASY FICTION, TAKE NOTE: This book is written from an animistic perspective, but takes the religious debate a step further: I would argue that it is anti-organized-religion. The above-mentioned critically-acclaimed and historically-beloved fantasy series all feature magic and sorcery, and conveniently ignore any question of religion, or attempt to reconcile religion with the content of the story. They also all rely heavily on animistic elements and some religious typing, with a savior-figure who either has deity and sovereignty (Aslan), or on whom the salvation of the known world relies (Harry and Aragorn). That's all ok with me, because it allows a religious person to read and enjoy the story without having to reconcile "magic" and "religion." But Wildwood takes a different tack: It's clear that Meloy has no use for a monotheistic god ('"Gods rest her soul," he said'), or for religion in general ("I know she wouldn't go in fer that claptrap, the gods and all, but I says it anyways." [p.255]). It takes a special disdain for religion and the religious to so infuse that tone into one's work that it's actually insulting to the reader, and he manages to convey that disdain.<br /><br />Overall, I just found the book disappointing (especially because his prose is still lovely and readable - Meloy IS actually a good writer). I don't expect a book to cater to me, and I enjoy reading different perspectives. If he'd simply wanted to write a book glorifying nature and vilifying industry, and encapsulate that philosophy in a fiction work, it would probably have been enjoyable. But that isn't this book, and this book left me completely dissatisfied.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8982713818637505543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1743843067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1743843067" />
    <a title="Kelly Bunch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18343811-kelly-bunch"><img alt="Kelly Bunch" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1743843067?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Bunch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Bunch" href="/user/show/18343811-kelly-bunch">Kelly Bunch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18343811-kelly-bunch?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1743843067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1086601587897097797">This second installment in the Wildwood series was just as magical as the previous book. I had my doubts after finishing book one that I would enjoy book two as much as I did. The size was honestly daunting even to me. <br/><br/>This sense has kind of been niggling at the back of my mind while I've been reading it, like there was something off about it that I couldn't quite place. While I enjoyed the first book and enjoyed it's mood which to me was similar to Chronicles of Narnia in its magical atmosphere</span>
  <span id="freeText1086601587897097797" style="display:none">This second installment in the Wildwood series was just as magical as the previous book. I had my doubts after finishing book one that I would enjoy book two as much as I did. The size was honestly daunting even to me. <br /><br />This sense has kind of been niggling at the back of my mind while I've been reading it, like there was something off about it that I couldn't quite place. While I enjoyed the first book and enjoyed it's mood which to me was similar to Chronicles of Narnia in its magical atmosphere I realized the other books that it reminded me of. They definitely have a dash of Grimm's fairy tales. While the main characters are children who are faced with real danger I guess what makes it seem darker to me is that it isn't always easy to tell friend from foe. Who is trustworthy and who is lying? What is safe and what's a trap? There is an unsettling unrest that keeps the reader both anxious for the characters' wellbeing and also completely glued to the story to see what will happen next. Personally, I find it keeps me from really enjoying the magic but I tend to enjoy the lighter side of fantasy books overall. <br /><br />I think the only other thing that I didn't enjoy was the Unthank Home. I have been in childcare related jobs for most of my life and I love working with children. Therefore, it is really difficult for me to read about anything that is injurious to children. Without spoilers there wasn't anything extreme or graphic just a very bleak reality and lack of care for children which is always really difficult for me to read about. However, it does seem incredibly important not only to this installment but also to the next so I'll be curious to see how it resolves. <br /><br />I definitely think I'll have to pick up (borrow) the last book in the series soon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1086601587897097797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_424181621" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/424181621" />
    <a title="Juushika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/616321-juushika"><img alt="Juushika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541586729p2/616321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/424181621?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juushika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juushika" href="/user/show/616321-juushika">Juushika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=genre-mg-and-ya">genre-mg-and-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=status-owned">status-owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer424181621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1747204978669126419">Since the events in <i>Wildwood</i>, Prue has returned to the unfulfilling monotony of the Outside while Curtis trains with bandits in the Wood. But their lives are disrupted again, this time by an assassination attempt which sends them on a long quest to resurrect a ruler and save the Wood. <i>Under Wildwood</i> continues the stylistic traditions of its predecessor, but this is a darker book. Rambling and whimsical, lengthy but so diverse--exploring new areas of the map and introducing a number of new charac</span>
  <span id="freeText1747204978669126419" style="display:none">Since the events in <i>Wildwood</i>, Prue has returned to the unfulfilling monotony of the Outside while Curtis trains with bandits in the Wood. But their lives are disrupted again, this time by an assassination attempt which sends them on a long quest to resurrect a ruler and save the Wood. <i>Under Wildwood</i> continues the stylistic traditions of its predecessor, but this is a darker book. Rambling and whimsical, lengthy but so diverse--exploring new areas of the map and introducing a number of new characters--that it never drags, it affects an almost mythical tone. But this view of Wildwood and its surroundings is starker, darker, and far more grim--not a new direction to take a children's series, but one that contrasts and compliments the whimsy and highlights the book's surprisingly vivid emotional landscape. Ellis's illustrations are the ideal companion, folksy and stylized but rendered suitably in thick blacks shot through with bright red.<br /><br />Unfortunately, <i>Under Wildwood</i> also does what I hate most about series and ends halfway, with the third book promising to finish up this particular quest. The comperably involved, extended journey suits the darker tone, but I'd still prefer a finished story; this is why I tend to avoid series. But I'm invested in Wildwood, enjoyed this installation, and will see it through. I don't believe these are new classics, but they have a certain beauty, especially for a St. John's resident: the location shines, as much a character as Prue or Curtis, and the series has a well-defined, unique tone that refuses to grow stagnant. I recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1747204978669126419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_878041262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/878041262" />
    <a title="Hollowspine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2069761-hollowspine"><img alt="Hollowspine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472602537p2/2069761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/878041262?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hollowspine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hollowspine" href="/user/show/2069761-hollowspine">Hollowspine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780062047083" href="/book/show/15818972-under-wildwood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2069761-hollowspine?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer878041262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12945808046074652318">3.5<br/><br/>The sequel to Wildwood takes place only a few months after the action of the first story. For Prue and Curtis however, it seems a lot longer. The story at first rotates between the two characters, Prue back in Portland living a dull life and daydreaming about her time in the IW. Curtis, on the other hand, has formed a new family among the Wildwood bandits.<br/><br/>Although I really enjoyed listening to Meloy's narration, I didn't enjoy Under Wildwood as much as the first book. It felt rushed at points</span>
  <span id="freeText12945808046074652318" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />The sequel to Wildwood takes place only a few months after the action of the first story. For Prue and Curtis however, it seems a lot longer. The story at first rotates between the two characters, Prue back in Portland living a dull life and daydreaming about her time in the IW. Curtis, on the other hand, has formed a new family among the Wildwood bandits.<br /><br />Although I really enjoyed listening to Meloy's narration, I didn't enjoy Under Wildwood as much as the first book. It felt rushed at points, but also meandered at other times. Some of the kid's dialog got a bit silly (they took turns one trying to explain something the other saying, "Hold up..." just like that too. No, "Wait a minute," or "Whaaat??" or anything other than "Hold up..." there cowboy.<br /><br />The story of the Dowager Governess in the first book wasn't happy go lucky, but Under Wildwood takes the darkness a bit further. I was a bit surprised the amount of blood shed throughout the book, especially adding vicious assassins to full out Mole war.<br /><br />I enjoyed the moles. I found them interesting characters in their world and especially as Gwendolyn reveals her own beliefs. However, I'm glad I listened to the audio version since the mole's speech is in all caps, which would get trying after a while.<br /><br />The ending too, left me a little confused. While the first novel ended really well, both concluding the plot of the novel, yet leaving enough to ponder on for the sequel, this second novel felt like it ended just as it began in the middle of the action.<br /><br />Overall, not as strong as the first, but still enjoyable. I'll look forward to when the library gets the next book on audio.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12945808046074652318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_450433698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/450433698" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1458035-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300224226p2/1458035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/450433698?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1458035-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer450433698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14079640682957230324">Under Wildwood is the second recently released book in the Wildwood Chronicles a slated trilogy. I enjoyed the first book immensely, likening it to a contemporary Chronicles of Narnia but set in my own backyard of Portland, OR. It has a wonderful dark side I find so alluring in young adult literature, similar to Neal Gaiman. I wish I had reread the first book so it would have been a little fresher in my mind, it would have helped me jump into this book quicker. We again follow Prue on an adventu</span>
  <span id="freeText14079640682957230324" style="display:none">Under Wildwood is the second recently released book in the Wildwood Chronicles a slated trilogy. I enjoyed the first book immensely, likening it to a contemporary Chronicles of Narnia but set in my own backyard of Portland, OR. It has a wonderful dark side I find so alluring in young adult literature, similar to Neal Gaiman. I wish I had reread the first book so it would have been a little fresher in my mind, it would have helped me jump into this book quicker. We again follow Prue on an adventure into Wildwood fraught with adversaries and danger. Teamed with Curtis her former classmate, they navigate the tunnels under the mysterious woods to complete a task that will save the woods. This books introduces several new characters and brings back a few favors. The downside of this book is it falls inline with the typical middle of the series syndrome where the story is not fully wrapped up so it feels like a little bit of a filler book. Just a little, not enough for me to be indignant or anything. I can't wait for the last book to come out. These books are beautifully illustrated by the authors wife and they are wonderfully affordable. Seriously, Christmas is coming people!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14079640682957230324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1185511524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17572854773575387748">I downloaded this in audiobook format from my library's website late one night, in the throes of severe insomnia and desperate for something to lull me to sleep.<br/><br/>Surely it can't be as bad as the first one, I thought to myself, and BOY WAS I WRONG.<br/><br/>Please stop, Colin Meloy. Your music is amazing and your glasses are totally happening, but your books are just so boring. So. Boring. If this had been written by a nobody, I highly doubt any publisher would have given it a second thought. It's like any </span>
  <span id="freeText17572854773575387748" style="display:none">I downloaded this in audiobook format from my library's website late one night, in the throes of severe insomnia and desperate for something to lull me to sleep.<br /><br />Surely it can't be as bad as the first one, I thought to myself, and BOY WAS I WRONG.<br /><br />Please stop, Colin Meloy. Your music is amazing and your glasses are totally happening, but your books are just so boring. So. Boring. If this had been written by a nobody, I highly doubt any publisher would have given it a second thought. It's like any other fantasy novel aimed at middle schoolers, but three times longer and not quite as good. It's like The Chronicles of Narnia and Peter Pan got blended together and spit out of some hipster's Vitamix. The mere fact that I made it all the way to the most awkwardly pretentious epilogue ever written, says more about my determination to finish than the actual book itself.<br /><br />However, 5 stars for putting me to sleep without fail. On that front, this book was invaluable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17572854773575387748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15239952-kinsey?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1814748562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10117918608315796099">A great sequel, in my opinion better than the first. The multiple story lines heightened suspense and enriched the complex world of Wildwood and the outside world of Portland. The new characters brought much needed additional perspectives and helped make the story's pace seem faster and more engaging than the first. Though a very long drawn out story, the author uses that time to provide more character depth and events to weave the web of saving Wildwood. It does feel like a distinct journey fro</span>
  <span id="freeText10117918608315796099" style="display:none">A great sequel, in my opinion better than the first. The multiple story lines heightened suspense and enriched the complex world of Wildwood and the outside world of Portland. The new characters brought much needed additional perspectives and helped make the story's pace seem faster and more engaging than the first. Though a very long drawn out story, the author uses that time to provide more character depth and events to weave the web of saving Wildwood. It does feel like a distinct journey from the first book, but the cliffhanger end connects it very closely with the events in the next book. Sometimes I was bogged down in the length and definitely felt more interested in some story lines than others, but I look forward to reading the next book to find out what happens to the many cast of characters and the magical Wildwood.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10117918608315796099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }

      Element.show('savingMessage')

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pM6Lfi1KQOZdHb5FolTYzrNFaGbV1bGAjoU+WBByYUWP87OFAKMF0vMzuxHylE2CKrq1Xa5m02VQykYKLXJ0Nw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/10741.Colin_Meloy">About Colin Meloy</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/10741.Colin_Meloy"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1546799884p3/10741.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/10741.Colin_Meloy">Colin Meloy

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2902729529921242901">Colin Patrick Henry Meloy is the lead singer and songwriter for the Portland, Oregon folk-rock band The Decemberists. In addition to his vocal duties, he plays acoustic guitar, 12-string acoustic guitar, electric guitar, bouzouki, and percussion. As of 2005, Meloy has written a 100-page book on The Replacements' fourth album, "Let It Be," released as part of the 33⅓ series.<br/><br/>Meloy was born in Helena</span>
  <span id="freeText2902729529921242901" style="display:none">Colin Patrick Henry Meloy is the lead singer and songwriter for the Portland, Oregon folk-rock band The Decemberists. In addition to his vocal duties, he plays acoustic guitar, 12-string acoustic guitar, electric guitar, bouzouki, and percussion. As of 2005, Meloy has written a 100-page book on The Replacements' fourth album, "Let It Be," released as part of the 33⅓ series.<br /><br />Meloy was born in Helena, Montana. His sister is Maile Meloy, an author often published in <i>The New Yorker</i>. He first attended the University of Oregon before transferring to the University of Montana, where he majored in creative writing. He then moved to Portland, where he met future bandmates Jenny Conlee and Nate Query. Prior to being in The Decemberists, Meloy was the lead singer and songwriter of Happy Cactus and Tarkio, both indie/folk bands from Montana.<br /><br />In early 2005, he embarked on his first solo tour in support of the self-released six-song EP, "Colin Meloy Sings Morrissey," which consists of six Morrissey covers. Only 1,000 copies of the album were made, and they were sold only on that tour. Meloy did a second solo tour in January 2006, playing with Laura Veirs and Amy Annelle. On this tour, he sold an EP featuring covers of British folk artist Shirley Collins. Shows from the 2006 tour were recorded for a live release. Meloy also appeared with Charlie Salas-Humara in the music video for "Pillar of Salt" by The Thermals.<br /><br />On February 24, 2006, Carson Ellis, Meloy's longtime girlfriend and graphic artist for the Decemberists, gave birth to their son, Henry "Hank" Meloy.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2902729529921242901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
